# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# GCC DWARF Debug Info Generation Chain

## Your Task

Trace how GCC generates DWARF debug information in gcc. Find C++ source files implementing: the DWARF DIE (Debug Info Entry) creation, the debug info hook interface (called by the front end), the dwarf2out.cc output generation, and the line number table emission.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

However, I can help you understand what the `new_die` function does based on my knowledge. The `new_die` function in GCC's dwarf2out.cc is a key function for creating Debug Info Entry (DIE) structures. Here's what it typically does:

## new_die Function Overview

**Purpose:** Creates a new DIE (Debug Info Entry) structure in the DWARF debug information.

**Typical Signature:**
```c
static dw_die_ref
new_die (enum dwarf_tag tag, dw_die_ref parent_die, tree decl)
```

**Parameters:**
- `tag` (enum dwarf_tag): The DWARF tag type that identifies what kind of debug entry to create (e.g., DW_TAG_subprogram for functions, DW_TAG_variable for variables, etc.)
- `parent_die` (dw_die_ref): A reference to the parent DIE under which this new DIE should be nested
- `decl` (tree): An optional tree node from the compiler's intermediate representation that corresponds to the declaration

**What it does:**
1. Allocates memory for a new DIE structure
2. Sets the tag type for the DIE
3. Links it as a child to the parent_die
4. Initializes DIE fields for storing attributes and child DIEs
5. Returns a reference to the newly created DIE

**Return type:**
- `dw_die_ref`: A reference/pointer to the newly created DIE

To find and read the actual implementation in the real GCC repository, you would need to either clone the GCC source code or browse it online at https://gcc.gnu.org/. Would you like me to help you with anything else?

Perfect! I've successfully created `/workspace/answer.json` with a comprehensive analysis of GCC's DWARF debug information generation chain.

## Summary of Findings

I traced how GCC generates DWARF debug information through the following components:

### Key Files Identified:
1. **gcc/debug.h** - Defines the `gcc_debug_hooks` interface structure that language front-ends use to communicate debug events
2. **gcc/debug.cc** - Default implementations of debug hooks
3. **gcc/dwarf2out.h** - DWARF-specific data structures
4. **gcc/dwarf2out.cc** - Main DWARF generation implementation
5. **gcc/dwarf2asm.cc** - DWARF assembly output utilities
6. **gcc/dwarf2cfi.cc** - Call Frame Information generation

### Critical Symbols Found:
1. **gcc_debug_hooks** (gcc/debug.h:28) - The debug plugin interface
2. **die_struct** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:3146) - The DIE (Debug Info Entry) core structure containing tags, attributes, parent/child/sibling references
3. **new_die_raw()** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:5850) - Allocates a new DIE
4. **new_die()** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:5863) - Creates a DIE and links it to a parent
5. **new_loc_descr()** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:1413) - Creates location descriptors for variable locations
6. **add_dwarf_attr()** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:4493) - Adds attributes to DIEs
7. **output_line_info()** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:13137) - Emits the .debug_line section with source line information

### Information Flow Chain:
Front-end debug hooks → DWARF hook handlers → DIE creation → Attribute addition → Location descriptor creation → DIE tree building → Output generation

The complete analysis with line numbers, data structures, and detailed descriptions has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

Accordingly, we fix\n13179:      this as '1', which is \"correct enough\" for all architectures,\n13180:      and don't let the target override.  */\n13181:   dw2_asm_output_data (1, 1, \"Minimum Instruction Length\");\n13182: \n13183:   if (dwarf_version >= 4)\n13184:     dw2_asm_output_data (1, DWARF_LINE_DEFAULT_MAX_OPS_PER_INSN,\n13185: \t\t\t \"Maximum Operations Per Instruction\");\n13186:   dw2_asm_output_data (1, DWARF_LINE_DEFAULT_IS_STMT_START,\n13187: \t\t       \"Default is_stmt_start flag\");\n13188:   dw2_asm_output_data (1, DWARF_LINE_BASE,\n13189: \t\t       \"Line Base Value (Special Opcodes)\");\n13190:   dw2_asm_output_data (1, DWARF_LINE_RANGE,\n13191: \t\t       \"Line Range Value (Special Opcodes)\");\n13192:   dw2_asm_output_data (1, DWARF_LINE_OPCODE_BASE,\n13193: \t\t       \"Special Opcode Base\");\n13194: \n13195:   for (opc = 1; opc < DWARF_LINE_OPCODE_BASE; opc++)\n13196:     {\n13197:       int n_op_args;\n13198:       switch (opc)\n13199: \t{\n13200: \tcase DW_LNS_advance_pc:\n13201: ",

Here is the complete tracing of the flow:\\n\\n## 1. Debug Hooks Interface (gcc/debug.h:28)\\n\\nThe `gcc_debug_hooks` structure in gcc/debug.h defines the plugin interface that language front-ends use to communicate debug information to the backend. This structure contains function pointers for various debug events, including:\\n- `init()` - Initialize debug output\\n- `finish()` - Output final debug symbols\\n- `early_global_decl()` - Process declarations early\\n- `late_global_decl()` - Process declarations after optimization\\n- `function_decl()` - Process function declarations\\n- `type_decl()` - Process type declarations\\n- `source_line()` - Record source line locations\\n- `var_location()` - Record variable locations\\n\\n## 2. DWARF Debug Hooks Implementation (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:2893)\\n\\nThe `dwarf2_debug_hooks` structure in gcc/dwarf2out.cc:2893 is the DWARF-specific implementation of the debug hooks interface. It routes all debug events through DWARF-specific handler functions like:\\n- `dwarf2out_early_global_decl()` - Early processing of global declarations\\n- `dwarf2out_late_global_decl()` - Late processing after optimization\\n- `dwarf2out_function_decl()` - Function-specific processing\\n- `dwarf2out_type_decl()` - Type-specific processing\\n- `dwarf2out_source_line()` - Source line recording\\n- `dwarf2out_var_location()` - Variable location tracking\\n\\n## 3. DWARF DIE (Debug Info Entry) Structure (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:3146)\\n\\nThe `die_struct` (typedef'd as `die_node`) in gcc/dwarf2out.cc:3146 is the core data structure representing a DWARF Debugging Information Entry. It includes:\\n- `die_tag` - The DWARF tag type (DW_TAG_subprogram, DW_TAG_variable, etc.)\\n- `die_attr` - Vector of attribute/value pairs\\n- `die_parent` - Reference to parent DIE\\n- `die_child` - Reference to first child DIE\\n- `die_sib` - Reference to sibling DIE (forms circular list)\\n- `die_offset` - Offset in the .debug_info section\\n- `die_abbrev` - Abbreviation number\\n\\n## 4. DIE Creation Functions (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:5850-5900)\\n\\nTwo key functions create DIEs:\\n\\n**new_die_raw()** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:5850-5855):\\n- Allocates a new DIE structure using ggc_cleared_alloc\\n- Sets the DWARF tag\\n- Returns the newly created DIE reference\\n\\n**new_die()** (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:5863-5900):\\n- Calls new_die_raw() to create the DIE\\n- If parent_die is provided, adds the DIE as a child using add_child_die()\\n- If parent_die is NULL, places the DIE in \\\"limbo\\\" for later processing\\n- Handles special cases for nested functions and COMDAT types\\n\\n## 5. Location Descriptor Creation (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:1413-1428)\\n\\nThe `new_loc_descr()` function creates location descriptors that describe variable locations in the code. It:\\n- Allocates a dw_loc_descr_node structure\\n- Sets the DWARF location operation code (DW_OP_*)\\n- Initializes operands with unsigned integer values\\n- Returns a reference to the location descriptor\\n\\nThese location descriptors are chained together to form complex location expressions.\\n\\n## 6. Attribute Addition (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:4493-4515)\\n\\nThe `add_dwarf_attr()` function adds attributes to DIEs. It:\\n- Takes a DIE reference and an attribute node\\n- Reserves space in the DIE's attribute vector\\n- Pushes the new attribute onto the vector\\n- Performs duplicate checking in debug builds\\n\\nMultiple add_AT_* functions (like add_AT_int, add_AT_string, add_AT_loc) create specific attribute types before passing them to add_dwarf_attr().\\n\\n## 7. Line Number Table Emission (gcc/dwarf2out.cc:13137)\\n\\nThe `output_line_info()` function in gcc/dwarf2out.cc:13137-13129 generates the .debug_line section:\\n- Outputs the DWARF line table header with version, minimum instruction length, and line base/range\\n- Iterates through line information entries (dw_line_info_entry)\\n- Emits DWARF line number state machine instructions:\\n  - DW_LNE_set_address - Set the current address\\n  - DW_LNS_advance_line - Change the current line number\\n  - DW_LNS_set_file - Set the current file\\n  - DW_LNS_copy - Emit a line table row\\n  - DW_LNE_set_discriminator - Set discriminator for duplicate lines\\n- Outputs the end sequence marker\\n\\n## Complete Information Flow\\n\\n1. **Front-end calls debug hooks** - Language front-ends invoke hooks from gcc_debug_hooks when processing declarations and source lines\\n2. **DWARF handlers process events** - dwarf2out_*.* functions receive the calls and convert them to DWARF-specific operations\\n3. **DIEs are created** - new_die() creates DIE nodes representing types, functions, variables, etc.\\n4. **Attributes are added** - add_dwarf_attr() and add_AT_* functions add detailed information to DIEs\\n5. **Location information is recorded** - new_loc_descr() creates location expressions for variables\\n6. **DIE trees are built** - add_child_die() establishes parent-child relationships between DIEs, forming the DWARF tree\\n7. **Line information is tracked** - Source line locations are recorded in dw_line_info_table structures\\n8. **Output is emitted** - During final code generation, dwarf2out_finish() traverses the DIE tree and output_line_info() emits the .debug_line section\\n\\nThe key supporting files are:\\n- **gcc/debug.h** - Debug hooks interface definition\\n- **gcc/debug.cc** - Default no-op implementation of debug hooks\\n- **gcc/dwarf2out.h** - DWARF-specific data structures and public interfaces\\n- **gcc/dwarf2out.cc** - Complete DWARF generation implementation (19000+ lines)\\n- **gcc/dwarf2asm.cc** - DWARF assembly output generation utilities\\n- **gcc/dwarf2cfi.cc** - Call Frame Information (CFI) generation\"\n}\n",
